## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt in a chemical reaction, which classically depends on the current concentration A through rate laws of various orders. Time t may appear explicitly if there are time-dependent external factors, autocatalytic mechanisms, or if the system involves integrated rate expressions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to concentration squared)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- First-order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (reversible first-order reaction approaching equilibrium)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * A) (self-catalyzed reaction)
- Reversible reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * (c2 + c3 * A) (forward and reverse reactions)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (transition between first and zero order)
- Competing reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (parallel first and second order pathways)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (rate with time-dependent activation)
- Fractal kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (heterogeneous or diffusion-limited reactions)
- Logistic-type: dA_dt = c0 * A * (1 + c1 * A) (growth with self-interaction)
- Square root kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5 (half-order reaction, surface catalysis)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate constants indicate consumption/decay of the species, positive indicate production — sign of leading coefficient determines if concentration increases or decreases
- Integer or half-integer reaction orders (0, 0.5, 1, 2, 3) arise from elementary reaction mechanisms and stoichiometry
- Rational function forms in concentration (A/(c+A)) indicate enzyme saturation or surface adsorption-limited kinetics (Langmuir-Hinshelwood mechanism)
- Product terms like A*(c-A) suggest reversible or equilibrium-approaching reactions where both forward and reverse rates matter
- Explicit time dependence in rate expressions often indicates photochemical reactions, temperature ramps, or catalyst deactivation
- Polynomial dependence on A (sum of A^n terms) suggests multiple parallel reaction pathways consuming the same species
- Fractional powers of concentration (A^0.5, A^1.5) indicate complex mechanisms involving radical intermediates or surface reactions
- If dA/dt depends only on A and not on t, the system is autonomous and the reaction follows a simple rate law with constant conditions

This has two terms: a $\sqrt{A}$ term and a $\sin(cA)$ term (with no phase shift, i.e., the sine term has zero phase offset).

**Candidate 4**: `A**0.5*c0 + A*c1 + A**c2*c3 + c4*sin(A*c5 + c6)`

This gives: $-0.10017\sqrt{A} + 0.47149\sin(0.85551A)$, which matches the GT. ✓

**Candidate 44**: `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A**c2*c3 + c4 + c5*sin(A*c6 + c7)`

This gives: $-0.10017\sqrt{A} + 0.47149\sin(0.85551A)$, which matches the GT. ✓

**Candidate 6**: `A**0.5*c0 + A**0.5*c1*sin(A*c2 + c3) + A**2*c4 + A*c5 + c6`

This has $\sqrt{A}\cdot\sin(\cdot)$ rather than plain $\sin(\cdot)$, so it cannot match exactly.

**Candidate 15**: `A**3*c0 + A**2*c1 + A*c2/(A + c3) + A + A**c4*c5 + c6*sin(A*c7 + c8)`

Set c0=0, c1=0, c2=0 (or handle the A term — there's a bare `A` term that can't be zeroed). The bare `+ A` cannot be eliminated, so this doesn't match unless we can cancel it. Setting c2/(A+c3) to cancel the 1... we'd need c2/(A+c3) = -1, which means c2 = -(A+c3), but that depends on A. With c4=0.5, c5=-0.10017 and the bare A: we'd need c2/(A+c3) = -1 for all A, which is impossible. No match.

**Candidate 41**: `A**3*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2*sin(...) + A + A**c5*c6*sin(...) + c9`

Has a bare `+ A` that can't be zeroed. Setting c1=-1 would give (c1+1)*A = 0... wait, it's `A*c1 + ... + A`, so that's `(c1+1)*A`. Multiple candidates match. The clearest matches are **Candidate 4** and **Candidate 44**, both of which can reproduce the GT exactly by appropriate parameter choices.
